79→ * functionality for accessing configs.\n    80→ */\n    81→public class ConfigDef {\n    82→\n    83→    private static final Pattern COMMA_WITH_WHITESPACE = Pattern.compile(\"\\\\s*,\\\\s*\");\n    84→\n    85→    /**\n    86→     * A unique Java object which represents the lack of a default value.\n    87→     */\n    88→    public static final Object NO_DEFAULT_VALUE = new Object();\n    89→\n    90→    private final Map<String, ConfigKey> configKeys;\n    91→    private final List<String> groups;\n    92→    private Set<String> configsWithNoParent;\n    93→\n    94→    public ConfigDef() {\n    95→        configKeys = new LinkedHashMap<>();\n    96→        groups = new LinkedList<>();\n    97→        configsWithNoParent = null;\n    98→    }\n    99→\n   100→    public ConfigDef(ConfigDef base) {\n   101→        configKeys = new LinkedHashMap<>(base.configKeys);\n   102→        groups = new LinkedList<>(base.groups);\n   103→        // It is not safe to copy this from the parent because we may subsequently add to the set of configs and\n   104→        // invalidate this\n   105→        configsWithNoParent = null;\n   106→    }\n   107→\n   108→    /**\n   109→     * Returns unmodifiable set of properties names defined in this {@linkplain ConfigDef}\n   110→     *\n   111→     * @return new unmodifiable {@link Set} instance containing the keys\n   112→     */\n   113→    public Set<String> names() {\n   114→        return Collections.unmodifiableSet(configKeys.keySet());\n   115→    }\n   116→\n   117→    public Map<String, Object> defaultValues() {\n   118→        Map<String, Object> defaultValues = new HashMap<>();\n   119→        for (ConfigKey key : configKeys.values()) {\n   120→            if (key.defaultValue != NO_DEFAULT_VALUE)\n   121→                defaultValues.put(key.name, key.defaultValue);\n   122→        }\n   123→        return defaultValues;\n   124→    }\n   125→\n   126→    public ConfigDef define(ConfigKey key) {\n   127→        if (configKeys.containsKey(key.name)) {\n   128→            throw new ConfigException(\"Configuration \" + key.name + \" is defined twice.\");\n   129→        }\n   130→        if (key.group != null && !groups.contains(key.group)) {\n   131→            groups.add(key.group);\n   132→        }\n   133→        configKeys.put(key.name, key);\n   134→        return this;\n   135→    }\n   136→\n   137→    /**\n   138→     * Define a new configuration\n   139→     * @param name          the name of the config parameter\n   140→     * @param type          the type of the config\n   141→     *  * @param orderInGroup  the order of this config in the group\n   147→     * @param width         the width of the config\n   148→     * @param displayName   the name suitable for display\n   149→     * @param dependents    the configurations that are dependents of this configuration\n   150→     * @param recommender   the recommender provides valid values given the parent configuration values\n   151→     * @return This ConfigDef so you can chain calls\n   152→     */\n   153→    public ConfigDef define(String name, Type type, Object defaultValue, Validator validator, Importance importance, Kafka\\n\\n### Pattern Overview\\nApache Kafka uses a class-based configuration pattern (not annotation-based) for defining and documenting configuration properties. While the task refers to @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef 'annotations', these do not exist as Java annotations in the Kafka codebase. Instead, Kafka uses:\\n\\n1. **ConfigDef class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java): A class for specifying the set of expected configurations, with detailed metadata for each configuration key including name, type, default value, documentation, validator, importance level, group information, and dependency information.\\n\\n2. **ConfigKey inner class** (defined within ConfigDef.java, line 1237): A static inner class within ConfigDef that represents individual configuration keys with comprehensive metadata.\\n\\n3. **AbstractConfig class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java): Base class extended by configuration classes throughout Kafka that holds parsed and original configuration values.\\n\\n### Configuration Documentation Generators\\nKafka provides documentation generation tools that extract configuration information at runtime:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/PredicateDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates by reflecting on OVERVIEW_DOC and CONFIG_DEF static fields.\\n\\n- **TransformationDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/TransformationDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect transformations (Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey).\\n\\n### AbstractConfig Subclasses\\nThroughout the Kafka codebase, 53+ classes extend AbstractConfig and define CONFIG_DEF static fields for configuration management. Kafka\\n\\n### Pattern Overview\\nApache Kafka uses a class-based configuration pattern (not annotation-based) for defining and documenting configuration properties. While the task refers to @ConfigKey and @ConfigDef 'annotations', these do not exist as Java annotations in the Kafka codebase. Instead, Kafka uses:\\n\\n1. **ConfigDef class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java): A class for specifying the set of expected configurations, with detailed metadata for each configuration key including name, type, default value, documentation, validator, importance level, group information, and dependency information.\\n\\n2. **ConfigKey inner class** (defined within ConfigDef.java, line 1237): A static inner class within ConfigDef that represents individual configuration keys with comprehensive metadata.\\n\\n3. **AbstractConfig class** (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java): Base class extended by configuration classes throughout Kafka that holds parsed and original configuration values.\\n\\n### Configuration Documentation Generators\\nKafka provides documentation generation tools that extract configuration information at runtime:\\n\\n- **PredicateDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/PredicateDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect predicates by reflecting on OVERVIEW_DOC and CONFIG_DEF static fields.\\n\\n- **TransformationDoc** (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/tools/TransformationDoc.java): Generates HTML documentation for Kafka Connect transformations (Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey).\\n\\n### AbstractConfig Subclasses\\nThroughout the Kafka codebase, 53+ classes extend AbstractConfig and define CONFIG_DEF static fields for configuration management. Key categories include:\\n\\n**Client-side configurations:**\\n- AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig\\n\\n**Kafka Connect configurations:**\\n- ConverterConfig, SimpleHeaderConverter, MirrorClientConfig, ConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, RestServerConfig\\n- Converter implementations: ByteArrayConverter, BooleanConverter, NumberConverter\\n- Transform implementations: Cast, DropHeaders, ExtractField, Filter, Flatten, HeaderFrom, HoistField, InsertField, InsertHeader, MaskField, RegexRouter, ReplaceField, SetSchemaMetadata, TimestampConverter, TimestampRouter, ValueToKey\\n- Predicate implementations: HasHeaderKey, RecordIsTombstone, TopicNameMatches\\n\\n**Server-side configurations:**\\n- AbstractKafkaConfig, ServerConfigs, QuotaConfig, SocketServerConfigs, DelegationTokenManagerConfigs, KRaftConfigs, ReplicationConfigs, ClientMetricsConfigs, MetricConfigs, BrokerSecurityConfigs\\n\\n**Component-specific configurations:**\\n- GroupCoordinatorConfig, ShareGroupConfig, ShareCoordinatorConfig (coordinators)\\n- MetadataLogConfig, QuorumConfig (raft)\\n- LogConfig, CleanerConfig (storage)\\n- AddPartitionsToTxnConfig, TransactionLogConfig, TransactionStateManagerConfig (transaction coordinator)\\n- StreamsConfig, TopologyConfig (streams)\\n\\nThis pattern provides a declarative, strongly-typed approach to configuration management without requiring Java annotations, using reflection and static field discovery for documentation generation.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
